10.1016/j.jmp.2019.102284
The analysis of individual preference systems is generally conducted by the use of the mathematical theory of relations. One of the most usual and simplest formalizations of the notion of an individual’s preference system consists in identifying it with a binary relation on a ground set of alternatives. In keeping with tradition, such an identification is carried out also in the present paper. Admittedly, other more complex formalizations exist; for instance, a quite recent growing strand of the literature expresses an individual’s preference system by means of two consistently intertwined binary preference relations. 
                         1 
                       
                      
                         1 
                         See, for instance,  Giarlotta and Greco (2013)  and  Giarlotta and Watson (2017a)  – as well as the literature mentioned therein – ( Cerreia-Vioglio, Giarlotta, Greco, Maccheroni, & Marinacci, 2018; Giarlotta, 2014, 2015; Giarlotta & Watson, 2017b ) and also the two mimeos ( Cerreia-Vioglio & Ok, 2018; Nishimura & Ok, 2018 ). 
                       In effect, the analysis conducted in this work is not in contrast with such more complex formalizations.

Fishburn (1970a, p. 12)  deems the asymmetry of individual preference relations as a consistency criterion and as an obvious condition to be imposed. Indeed, preferences are asymmetric in the natural language: the assertion “I prefer  
                         x 
                       to  
                         y 
                      ” declared by an individual cannot simultaneously coexist with the assertion “I prefer  
                         y 
                       to  
                         x 
                      ” declared by that same individual. Even the Latin etymon  praeferre  – which means to put ( ferre ) before ( prae ) – of the English verb  to prefer  doubtless testifies to the asymmetric nature of preference relations. For this reason, in the first part of the paper, particular attention will be devoted directly to asymmetric relations, rather than on the asymmetric parts of not necessarily asymmetric relations.

Transitivity is a useful property and often employed in the theory of preference relations but, as a matter of fact, it is not an overall accepted property. This is particularly true for the transitivity of indifference in the precise sense of  Fishburn (1991, pp. 113–114) : 
                         2 
                       
                      
                         2 
                         Note that Fishburn’s transitivity of indifference is in fact the transitivity of incomparability with respect to the asymmetric part of a relation. 
                        Armstrong (1939, 1948, 1950) ,  Aumann (1962) ,  Fishburn (1970c) ,  Luce (1956)  and  Peleg (1970)  might be considered seminal contributions where the latter form of transitivity has been questioned and where preferences with intransitive indifference have begun to be systematically studied; also  Wiener (1914)  is often included in this list—see  Fishburn (1970b)  and  Fishburn and Monjardet (1992)  for additional references. 
                         3 
                       
                      
                         3 
                         A few of more recent papers (in addition to some of those already mentioned in fn.  1 ) are  Cantone, Giarlotta, Greco, and Watson (2016) ,  Dubra, Maccheroni, and Ok (2004) ,  Giarlotta and Watson (2014, 2018) ,  Nishimura (2018) ,  Ok (2002) ,  Öztürk (2008)  and  Pouzet and Zaguia (2019) . 
                       Strict weak orders (i.e., asymmetric and negatively transitive relations) are perhaps the most prominent examples of relations where transitivity of indifference holds.

Even the transitivity of the asymmetric part of a preference relation is not immune from criticism: see also  Fishburn (1991)  for a long discussion. However, such a kind of transitivity is generally considered much more plausible than the transitivity of indifference. In an already mentioned article – see again  Fishburn (1970a, p.12)  – Fishburn labels the transitivity of asymmetric preference relations as a reasonable criterion of coherence. However, as a matter of fact, a formal identification of asymmetric and transitive relations with coherent ones have never been formally advanced.

As it will be shown in the coming sections, every strict weak order is a coherent order. However, the converse is generally false. For instance, the canonical orders of  
                         
                            
                               Z 
                            
                            
                               n 
                            
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            
                               Q 
                            
                            
                               n 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               R 
                            
                            
                               n 
                            
                         
                       discussed in Section  5  possess irreflexive parts which are coherent orders but not strict weak orders when  
                         
                            n 
                            ≥ 
                            2 
                         
                       and – just to provide additional prominent examples – the first-order stochastic dominance relation and many Pareto dominance relations discussed in Section  7  possess irreflexive parts which are coherent orders but not strict weak orders. On finite ground sets, though, coherent orders and strict weak orders coincide. As these preliminary results evidence, there exist important connections between coherent orders and strict weak orders. The main objective of this work is studying the conditions for a coherent relation to be a strict weak order and for a transitive relation to be coherent.

The paper is organized as follows. Section  2  fixes the notation, recalls some standard definitions and conveniently states some results about transitive relations. Section  3  presents a characterization of strict partial orders. Building on it, Section  4  introduces the notion of a coherent relation and proves that a relation on a finite ground set is a strict weak order if and only if it is coherent and that a Ferrers relation is a strict weak order if and only if it is coherent. Section  4  examines also the restrictions of coherent relations. Section  5  shows purely order-theoretic conditions for the irreflexive part of a partial order to possess a coherent irreflexive part. Section  6  inquires into the sufficiency of some additional conditions of topological nature for a transitive relation to be coherent or to possess a coherent asymmetric part; it is proved, in particular, that under customary 
                         4 
                       
                      
                         4 
                         Customary, at least for the literature on consumers’ choices. 
                       continuity and nonsatiation assumptions each preorder has a coherent asymmetric part. Section  7  discusses two final examples. An  Appendix  contains all lemmas of the paper.

Definition 1 
                            A relation  
                                  B 
                                on a ground set  
                                  X 
                                is: a  preorder  iff  
                                  B 
                                is reflexive and transitive; a  partial order  iff  
                                  B 
                                is an antisymmetric preorder; a  strict partial order  iff  
                                  B 
                                is asymmetric and transitive; an  interval order  iff  
                                  B 
                                is asymmetric and Ferrers; a  strict weak order  iff  
                                  B 
                                is asymmetric and negatively transitive. 
                                  6 
                                
                               
                                  6 
                                  In books like, e.g.,  Aleskerov, Bouyssou, and Monjardet (2007) ,  Bridges and Mehta (1995)  and  Schmidt (2010) , one can find an overview of several properties of the orders just defined.

                                  B

Proof 
                            A consequence of  Theorems 1 and 2 . ■

A consequence of  Theorems 1 and 2 . ■

Theorem 3  characterizes strict partial order relations. It is left to the reader to compare its statement with that of  Theorem 2  and with that of  Corollary 1 . While it is reasonable to conjecture that  Theorem 3  is known, I do not have a reference for it; at any rate, such a basic result is so important for the sequel that it is worth to be enunciated and proved.

Theorem 3 
                         
                            Let  
                            
                               B 
                             
                            be a relation on a set  
                            
                               X 
                            
                            . Assertions I to III are equivalent. 
                         
                         
                            
                               
                                  
                                     I. 
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is irreflexive and transitive. 
                                  
                               
                               
                                  
                                     II. 
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           ∀ 
                                           
                                           y 
                                           , 
                                           x 
                                           ∈ 
                                           X 
                                           : 
                                           y 
                                           ∈ 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              
                                                 x 
                                              
                                           
                                           ⇒ 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              
                                                 y 
                                              
                                           
                                           ⊂ 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              
                                                 x 
                                              
                                           
                                        
                                     
                                     . 
                                  
                               
                               
                                  
                                     III. 
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict partial order.

We now define as “coherent relations” those which satisfy the one-way implication displayed in part II of  Theorem 3  as a double implication. Such relations will often be alternatively referred to as “coherent orders”.

Definition 2 
                         A relation  
                               B 
                             on a set  
                               X 
                             is  coherent  iff  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        ∀ 
                                        
                                        y 
                                        , 
                                        x 
                                        ∈ 
                                        X 
                                        : 
                                        y 
                                        ∈ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              x 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⇔ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              y 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⊂ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           ( 
                                           x 
                                           ) 
                                        
                                        .

A relation  
                               B 
                             on a set  
                               X 
                             is  coherent  iff  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        ∀ 
                                        
                                        y 
                                        , 
                                        x 
                                        ∈ 
                                        X 
                                        : 
                                        y 
                                        ∈ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              x 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⇔ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              y 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⊂ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           ( 
                                           x 
                                           ) 
                                        
                                        .

By virtue of  Theorem 3 , it is obvious that every coherent relation is also a strict partial order.  Theorem 4  shows that every strict weak order is a coherent relation and hence that such a type of relation is intermediate between the two mentioned orders.

Theorem 4 
                         
                            Let  
                            
                               B 
                             
                            be a relation on a set  
                            
                               X 
                            
                            . 
                         
                         
                            
                               
                                  
                                     1. 
                                  
                                  
                                     If  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict weak order then  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is coherent. 
                                  
                               
                               
                                  
                                     2. 
                                  
                                  
                                     If  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is coherent then  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict partial order.

Let  
                            
                               B 
                             
                            be a relation on a set  
                            
                               X 
                            
                            .

1. 
                                  
                                  
                                     If  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict weak order then  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is coherent.

                                     If  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is coherent then  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict partial order.

If  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict weak order then  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is coherent.

If  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is coherent then  
                                     
                                        B 
                                      
                                     is a strict partial order.

Proof 
                         1. Suppose  
                               B 
                             is a strict weak order. Any strict weak order is a strict partial order. 
                               8

                             So  
                               B 
                             is a strict partial order and  Theorem 3  implies that

                                        X

                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              x

                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              y 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⊂ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              x 
                                           
                                        
                                        . 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            To conclude the proof it suffices to show that  
                               
                                  (5) 
                                  
                                     
                                        ∀ 
                                        
                                        y 
                                        , 
                                        x 
                                        ∈ 
                                        X 
                                        : 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              y 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⊂ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              x 
                                           
                                        
                                        ⇒ 
                                        y 
                                        ∈ 
                                        B 
                                        
                                           
                                              x 
                                           
                                        
                                        . 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            Suppose  
                               
                                  y 
                                  , 
                                  x 
                                  ∈ 
                                  X 
                               
                             and  
                               
                                  B 
                                  
                                     
                                        y

Examples 1 and 2  show that a coherent relation on an infinite ground set need not be a strict weak order: whether or not the ground set is uncountably infinite is immaterial.  Theorem 6  proves that finite coherent relations are strict weak orders.

Theorem 6 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a relation on a set  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               and suppose  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               is finite. Assertions I and II are equivalent. 
                            
                            
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        I. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is a strict weak order. 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        II. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is coherent.

Let  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a relation on a set  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               and suppose  
                               
                                  X

I. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is a strict weak order.

                                           B 
                                         
                                        is coherent.

B 
                                         
                                        is a strict weak order.

B 
                                         
                                        is coherent.

Example 2  shows that a coherent relation need not be a strict weak order;  Example 3  shows that a strictly partially ordered Ferrers relation need not be a strict weak order. However, coherent Ferrers relations are strict weak orders.  Theorem 7  and its  Corollary 2  prove this fact.

                                        II.

Corollary 2 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a relation on a set  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Assertions I to III are equivalent. 
                            
                            
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        I. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is a strict weak order. 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        II. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is a coherent interval order. 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        III. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is coherent and Ferrers.

Let  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a relation on a set  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Assertions I to III are equivalent.

I. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is a strict weak order. 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        II. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is a coherent interval order. 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     
                                        III. 
                                     
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                         
                                        is coherent and Ferrers.

B 
                                         
                                        is a strict weak order.

B 
                                         
                                        is a coherent interval order.

B 
                                         
                                        is coherent and Ferrers.

Proof 
                            Any strict weak order is Ferrers. 
                                  12 
                                
                               
                                  12 
                                  See, e.g., Proposition 12.9 in  Schmidt (2010)  for a proof of this fact. 
                                So the implication I 
                                  ⇒ 
                               II follows from  Theorem 4 . The implication II 
                                  ⇒ 
                               III follows from the definition of an interval order. The implication III 
                                  ⇒ 
                               I follows from  Theorem 7 . ■

Any strict weak order is Ferrers.

                                  ⇒

Any restriction of a strict partial order relation is still a strict partial order relation and any restriction of strict weak order relation is still a strict weak order relation. To the contrary, the restriction of a coherent relation to some proper subset of its ground set need not be coherent: to check this claim it suffices to note that the relation illustrated in  Example 3  is not coherent and that such a relation is the restriction to the set  
                            
                               { 
                               0 
                               , 
                               2 
                               , 
                               3 
                               } 
                            
                          of the coherent relation illustrated in  Example 1 . Nevertheless, we can show the validity of the following  Theorem 8 .

                                           , 
                                           y 
                                           ∈ 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              ( 
                                              x 
                                              ) 
                                           
                                           : 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              ( 
                                              z 
                                              ) 
                                           
                                           ⊂ 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              ( 
                                              y 
                                              ) 
                                           
                                           ⇒ 
                                           z 
                                           ∈ 
                                           B 
                                           
                                              ( 
                                              y 
                                              ) 
                                           
                                           . 
                                        
                                     
                                  
                               But  (31)  is readily seen to be true because of the coherence of  
                                  B 
                               . ■

Section  5  shows purely order-theoretic conditions for the irreflexive part of a partial order to be coherent. For sake of clarity, some preliminary standard notions are briefly recalled and the definition of a canonical partial order is explicitly formulated. Let  
                         B 
                       be a partial order relation on a set  
                         X 
                       and let  
                         S 
                       be a subset of  
                         X 
                      : an element  
                         x 
                       in  
                         X 
                       is a  lower bound  of  
                         S 
                       iff  
                         
                            s 
                            ∈ 
                            B 
                            
                               ( 
                               x 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            s 
                            ∈ 
                            S 
                         
                      ; an element  
                         x 
                       in  
                         X 
                       is an  upper  
                      bound  of  
                         S 
                       iff  
                         
                            x 
                            ∈ 
                            B 
                            
                               ( 
                               s 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            s 
                            ∈ 
                            S 
                         
                      ; a lower bound  
                         y 
                       of  
                         S 
                       is an  infimum  of  
                         S 
                       iff  
                         
                            y 
                            ∈ 
                            B 
                            
                               ( 
                               x 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       for each lower bound  
                         x 
                       of  
                         S 
                      ; an upper bound  
                         y 
                       of  
                         S 
                       is a  supremum  of  
                         S 
                       iff  
                         
                            x 
                            ∈ 
                            B 
                            
                               ( 
                               y 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       for each upper bound  
                         x 
                       of  
                         S 
                      ; an infimum  
                         y 
                       of  
                         S 
                       is a  minimum  of  
                         S 
                       iff  
                         
                            y 
                            ∈ 
                            S 
                         
                      . A pair  
                         
                            ( 
                            X 
                            , 
                            B 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a  lattice  iff  
                         B 
                       is a partial order relation on  
                         X 
                       such that the infimum and the supremum of

                            y

                       for all

                            X

                            X

Theorem 9  provides purely order-theoretic sufficient conditions for a partial order to possess a coherent irreflexive part.  Example 4  shows that many spaces of basic importance for mathematics satisfy those conditions.

Theorem 9

                               has no minimum. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is coherent.

Open-valued and closed-valued relations – possibly undermany other alternative names – are frequently employed in the literature on preference relations. Each of them, per se, expresses a weak notion of continuity. 
                         13 
                       
                      
                         13 
                         In general, however, open-valuedness is imposed on strict partial orders while closed-valuedness on preorders. 
                       To the best of my knowledge, the definition of a capacious relation is new. Also capaciousness is an expression of a weak notion of continuity. Indeed, in the  Appendix  the following results are shown to be true. If we restrict attention to a – possibly but not necessarily reflexive – transitive relation  
                         B 
                       then the condition of capaciousness of  
                         B 
                       is more general than closed-valuedness of  
                         B 
                      :  Lemma 3  in the  Appendix  guarantees that every transitive and closed-valued relation is capacious. If instead we restrict attention to a coherent relation  
                         B 
                       then the condition of capaciousness of  
                         B 
                       is more general than the open-valuedness of  
                         
                            
                               B 
                            
                            
                               − 
                               1 
                            
                         
                      :  Lemma 4  in the  Appendix  guarantees that every coherent relation with an open-valued inverse is capacious.

Nonsatiation and local nonsatiation are two notions frequently employed in the literature on preference relations, especially the economic one. Evidently, local nonsatiation implies nonsatiation. Both definitions call for the nonexistence of maximal elements for

Quasi-nonsatiation requires the asymmetric part of a relation to satisfy the condition enunciated by part 1 of  Theorem 5  and so, in a sense, quasi-nonsatiation has already been tacitly introduced in Section  4  . The mentioned result guarantees that every coherent relation – and hence every strict weak order relation – is quasi-nonsatiated. Evidently, local nonsatiation implies nonsatiation and the latter implies quasi-nonsatiation. It is readily seen also that local nonsatiation implies local quasi-nonsatiation and that the latter in turn implies quasi-nonsatiation. The mentioned implications are conveniently summarized by  Fig. 1 .

Coherence is satisfied by the asymmetric part of any transitive, capacious and locally quasi-nonsatiated relation.  Theorem 10  proves this claim.

Theorem 10 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a transitive relation on  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is capacious and locally quasi-nonsatiated. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is coherent.

Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B

                                  X

                               . So

Examples 7 and 8  are taken from  Aumann (1962, Sect. 3) .  Example 7  shows a relation satisfying all conditions of  Theorem 10 .  Example 8  shows that in  Theorem 10  the capaciousness assumption cannot be simply dropped.

From  Theorem 10  we obtain  Corollaries 4 and 5 .  Corollary 4  is a not-so-direct consequence of  Theorem 10  that makes a crucial use of  Lemma 3  in the  Appendix : the closed-valuedness of a transitive relation as well as its local quasi-nonsatiation – in particular, under the stronger form of local nonsatiation – are frequently used in the theoretical literature on consumers’ choices. 
                            14 
                          
                         
                            14 
                            For a discussion on these conditions the reader is referred to  Mas-Colell, Whinston, and Green (1995)  and to the already cited  Bridges and Mehta (1995) . 
                         
                         Corollary 5  is an almost direct consequence of  Theorem 10 .

Corollary 4 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a transitive relation on  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is closed-valued and locally quasi-nonsatiated. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is coherent.

Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a transitive relation on  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is closed-valued and locally quasi-nonsatiated. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is coherent.

Proof 
                            Note that  
                                  
                                     (39) 
                                     
                                        
                                           
                                              
                                                 
                                                    ( 
                                                    
                                                       
                                                          B 
                                                       
                                                       
                                                          A 
                                                       
                                                    
                                                    ) 
                                                 
                                              
                                              
                                                 A 
                                              
                                           
                                           = 
                                           
                                              
                                                 B 
                                              
                                              
                                                 A 
                                              
                                           
                                           . 
                                        
                                     
                                  
                               Part 1 of  Lemma 1  in the  Appendix  implies the transitivity of  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                               .  Lemma 3  in the  Appendix  ensures that  
                                  B 
                                is capacious. By virtue of  (39) , the capaciousness of  
                                  B 
                                is equivalent to the capaciousness of  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                and the local quasi-nonsatiation of  
                                  B 
                                is equivalent to the local quasi-nonsatiation of  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                               
                               .  So  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A

                                           ( 
                                           
                                              
                                                 B 
                                              
                                              
                                                 A 
                                              
                                           
                                           ) 
                                        
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                               . So  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                is coherent by  (39) . ■

Corollary 5 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a strict partial order relation (resp. an interval order relation) on 
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is capacious and locally quasi-nonsatiated. Then  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is a coherent (resp. a strict weak order) relation.

Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a strict partial order relation (resp. an interval order relation) on 
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is capacious and locally quasi-nonsatiated. Then  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is a coherent (resp. a strict weak order) relation.

Proof 
                            Any interval order relation is a strict partial order. 
                                  15 
                                
                               
                                  15 
                                  See, e.g., Proposition 12.6 in  Schmidt (2010)  for a proof of this assertion. 
                                Thus  Theorem 10  guarantees the coherence of  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                               . The asymmetry of  
                                  B 
                                implies  
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                        
                                        
                                           A 
                                        
                                     
                                     = 
                                     B 
                                  
                                and so  
                                  B 
                                is coherent.  Corollary 2  guarantees that  
                                  B 
                                is even a strict weak order when  
                                  B 
                                is an interval order relation. ■

Any interval order relation is a strict partial order. 
                                  15 
                                
                               
                                  15 
                                  See, e.g., Proposition 12.6 in  Schmidt (2010)  for a proof of this assertion. 
                                Thus  Theorem 10  guarantees the coherence of  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                               . The asymmetry of  
                                  B 
                                implies  
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           B 
                                        
                                        
                                           A 
                                        
                                     
                                     = 
                                     B 
                                  
                                and so  
                                  B 
                                is coherent.  Corollary 2  guarantees that  
                                  B 
                                is even a strict weak order when  
                                  B 
                                is an interval order relation. ■

Examples 9 and 10  display instances of relations that satisfy the conditions of  Corollaries 4 and 5 . As is evident from  Example 9 , the conditions of  Corollary 4  – and so those of  Theorem 10  – are certainly compatible with disconnected ground sets.

A classical result of the literature about the sufficient (but not necessary) conditions for a relation to be a strict weak order is due to  Schmeidler (1971) . The following assertion is the statement of Proposition ( 
                            ∗ 
                         ) in the proof of the Theorem in  Schmeidler (1971) .

Theorem 11 
                            
                               Schmeidler, 1971 
                            
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a transitive relation on  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               is connected, 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is closed-valued and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is open-valued. Besides suppose  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        − 
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is closed-valued and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           ( 
                                           
                                              
                                                 B 
                                              
                                              
                                                 − 
                                                 1 
                                              
                                           
                                           ) 
                                        
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is open-valued. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is a strict weak order relation.

Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and

                               is connected, 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is closed-valued and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is open-valued. Besides suppose  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        − 
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is closed-valued and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           ( 
                                           
                                              
                                                 B 
                                              
                                              
                                                 − 
                                                 1 
                                              
                                           
                                           ) 
                                        
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is open-valued. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is a strict weak order relation.

Theorem 12  parallels Schmeidler’s Theorem for the case of coherent relations. Before enunciating  Theorem 12 , it is worth to remark that the assumptions of Schmeidler’s Theorem imply the quasi-nonsatiation of  
                            B 
                         . 
                            18 
                          
                         
                            18 
                            Such an implication is due to the simple fact that, under the assumptions of Schmeidler’s Theorem,  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                is a strict weak order and any strict weak order is quasi-nonsatiated. 
                          Therefore any relation satisfying the assumptions of that result satisfies also the assumptions of  Theorem 12 .  Examples 11 and 12  will show that the converse is false in general.

Theorem 12 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a transitive relation on  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               is connected, 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is closed-valued and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is open-valued. Besides suppose  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is quasi-nonsatiated. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is coherent.

Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and

Corollary 6  concludes showing sufficient conditions for  
                            
                               
                                  B 
                               
                               
                                  A 
                               
                            
                          to be a strict weak order. It is worth to remark that Schmeidler’s Theorem not only implies the quasi-nonsatiation of  
                            B 
                          – and this has been already remarked above – but also that  
                            
                               
                                  B 
                               
                               
                                  A 
                               
                            
                          is Ferrers. 
                            19 
                          
                         
                            19 
                            This last implication is due to the simple fact that, under the assumptions of Schmeidler’s Theorem,  
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                is a strict weak order and any strict weak order is Ferrers. 
                          Therefore, any relation satisfying the assumptions of Schmeidler’s Theorem satisfies also the assumptions of  Corollary 6 .  Example 12  will show that the converse is false in general.

Corollary 6 
                            
                               Let  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               be a set endowed with some topology and  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               be a transitive relation on  
                               
                                  X 
                               
                               . Suppose  
                               
                                  X 
                                
                               is connected, 
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is closed-valued and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is open-valued. Besides suppose  
                               
                                  B 
                                
                               is quasi-nonsatiated and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is Ferrers. Then  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        B 
                                     
                                     
                                        A 
                                     
                                  
                                
                               is a strict weak order relation.

Proof 
                            A consequence of  Theorems 7 and 12 . ■

A consequence of  Theorems 7 and 12 . ■

Example 11  shows that the conditions of  Theorem 12  are sufficient for the asymmetric part of a relation to be coherent but not, in general, to be a strict weak order.  Example 12  shows an instance of a strict weak order satisfying all assumptions of  Corollary 6  – and so those of  Theorem 12  – which does not satisfy some assumptions of Schmeidler’s Theorem.

Important examples of lattices possessing irreflexive parts that are coherent orders – but that are not strict weak orders in general – have already been shown in Section  5 . In Section  7  we consider two more examples of coherent orders that are not strict weak orders in general: first-order stochastic dominance relation and (some) Pareto dominance relations. Such dominance relations are often used in the literature – see, e.g.,  Ok (2002)  – to motivate the interest in “incomplete preferences” (or, more precisely, in preorder relations for which at least two elements of the ground sets are not mutually related). An analogous use is made here to motivate the interest in coherent orders.

First-order stochastic dominance orders are of importance to economics and decision theory.  Example 13  – taken from  Ok (2007, p. 109)  – considers the first-order stochastic dominance relation on the set

                          alternatives. Though immaterial for the discussion below, it is assumed that the higher the number associated with an alternative the higher is the monetary return generated by the alternative.

                               ε 
                               ⋅ 
                               
                                  
                                     e 
                                  
                                  
                                     n 
                                  
                               
                               ∈ 
                               
                                  
                                     B 
                                  
                                  
                                     A 
                                  
                               
                               
                                  ( 
                                  x 
                                  ) 
                               
                            
                          for all sufficiently small  
                            
                               ε 
                               > 
                               0

                               x 
                               ≠ 
                               
                                  
                                     e 
                                  
                                  
                                     n 
                                  
                               
                            
                         ; we can conclude that  
                            B 
                          is locally quasi-nonsatiated. Also, it can be noted that  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     B 
                                     
                                        ( 
                                        x 
                                        ) 
                                     
                                     = 
                                     
                                        
                                           ⋂ 
                                        
                                        
                                           k 
                                           = 
                                           1 
                                        
                                        
                                           n 
                                           − 
                                           1 
                                        
                                     
                                     
                                        { 
                                        z

                                              R 
                                           
                                           
                                              n

                                     ∩ 
                                     
                                        
                                           Δ 
                                        
                                        
                                           n 
                                           − 
                                           1 
                                        
                                     
                                  
                               
                            
                         and so that  
                            
                               B 
                               
                                  ( 
                                  x 
                                  ) 
                               
                            
                          is a finite intersection of closed sets; we can conclude that  
                            B 
                          is closed-valued.  Corollary 4  ensures that  
                            
                               
                                  B 
                               
                               
                                  A 
                               
                            
                          is a coherent order.

Pareto dominance orders are of importance to economics, optimization and decision theory (in particular, to multi-criteria analysis). An elegant way to express the Pareto dominance relation makes use of cones: see for instance  Ehrgott (2005, Chapter 1)  about their use in multicriteria optimization. For the simple context of a Euclidean space,  Example 14  shows a class of cones inducing Pareto dominance orders with coherent irreflexive parts.

                            C

Lemma 3

                            is capacious.

Lemma 4 
                         
                            Let  
                            
                               X 
                             
                            be a set endowed with some topology and  
                            
                               B 
                             
                            be a relation on  
                            
                               X

                               B 
                             
                            is coherent and  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     B 
                                  
                                  
                                     − 
                                     1 
                                  
                               
                             
                            is open-valued then  
                            
                               B 
                             
                            is capacious.

Remark 5 
                         In  Lemma 4  the assumption of coherence cannot be simply dropped. For instance, putting
